Discount and Increase in Murabahah and Tawliyah
Explanation of rulings on discount and increase with illustrative cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissibility of discount and the principle of attachment of increase in murabahah contracts, and apply these rules to cases involving defects and preemption.

Core Idea
Discount after sale is valid by consensus; increase added to the sold item merges with the original contract.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira clarifies two important post-contract modifications in murabahah and tawliyah: discount (hatt) and increase (ziyada). It explains that discount is permissible even after the item is destroyed, and that any increase—whether in the item or price—attaches to the original contract, making it as if both were part of the initial agreement. The text then illustrates these principles through practical cases involving defect and preemption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two post-contract modifications
Discount (hatt) is a reduction in price after the sale; increase (ziyada) is an addition to the sold item or price after the contract. Both are permissible in murabahah and tawliyah sales.
These modifications affect the rights and obligations of the parties.
2
Understand the permissibility of discount
The text states that discount is permissible even after the subject matter is destroyed, by consensus (ijma'). This means the seller can reduce the price at any time, and the buyer is entitled to the reduced price.
Consensus (ijma') is a strong source of authority in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Grasp the principle of attachment of increase
When the seller adds an increase (e.g., an extra garment) or the buyer adds extra money after the contract, that increase attaches to the original subject matter. Legally, it is as if the contract from the beginning covered both the original and the increase.
This principle ensures that the increase is considered part of the same transaction for the purposes of options (khiyar) and other rights.
4
Apply to the defect scenario
If the seller adds a garment after the sale and the buyer later discovers a defect in one garment: before possession, the buyer can rescind the entire sale or accept all; after possession, the buyer can only return the defective item for its share of the price, even if the defect is in the added garment.
The option (khiyar al-'ayb) is affected by whether possession has occurred.
5
Apply to the preemption scenario
The preemptor (shafi') has the right to take the property by preemption after any discount has been applied. The discount reduces the price, and the preemptor pays the discounted amount.
Preemption (shuf'ah) is a right to acquire jointly owned property when one co-owner sells to a third party.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المرابحة والتولية ويجوز أن يحط من الثمن، ويتعلق الاستحقاق بجميع ذلك. أما الزيادة في المبيع بعد هلاك المبيع: ففي البقالي: يجوز، بخلاف الزيادة في الثمن. ولو قوله: ويجوز أن يحط من الثمن. حط بعد هلاك المعقود عليه: جاز، إجماعاً. قوله: ويتعلق الاستحقاق بجميع ذلك، أن الزيادة تلحق يعني بالمزيد عليه، فتصير مع المزيد عليه عوضاً لما يقابلها من المعقود عليه، فيجعل كأن العقد من الابتداء ورد عليهما. وببيانه في مسائل: منها: إذا اشترى عشرة أثواب بمائة درهم، فزاد البائع بعد العقد ثوباً، ثم اطلع المشتري على عيب في أحد الثياب: إن كان قبل القبض: فالمشتري بالخيار إن شاء فسخ البيع في جميعها، وإن شاء رضي بها. وإن كان بعد القبض: فله رد المعيب بحصته من الثمن وإن كانت الزيادة هي المعيبة. وكذا المشتري لو زاد البائع عشرة دراهم، فاستحق كلها: فللمشتري أن يرجع عليه بمائة وعشرة. كذا في الينابيع. ومنها: أن الشفيع يستحق الشفعة بما بقي بعد الحط.
Chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. It is permissible to reduce from the price, and the entitlement (for increase) attaches to all of that. As for the increase in the sold item after its destruction: in 'al-Baqqali', it is permissible, unlike the increase in the price. And if he said: 'It is permissible to reduce from the price.' Reduction after the destruction of the subject matter is permissible by consensus. He said: 'and the entitlement attaches to all of that' meaning the increase attaches to that which is increased, so it becomes together with the increased item a substitute for what corresponds to it from the subject matter, so it is as if the contract from the beginning applied to both. And its explanation is in cases: among them: if someone bought ten garments for one hundred dirhams, then the seller after the contract increased a garment, then the buyer discovered a defect in one of the garments: if before taking possession, the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may rescind the entire sale, and if he wishes, he may accept it. And if after taking possession, he has the right to return the defective item for its share of the price even if the increase is the defective one. Likewise, if the buyer increased ten dirhams and all was reclaimed, the buyer may reclaim one hundred and ten from him. Similarly in 'al-Yanabi''. Among them: that the preemptor is entitled to preemption for what remains after the reduction.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the rulings on discount (hatt) and increase (ziyada) in murabahah and tawliyah contracts. It states that it is permissible for the seller to reduce the price after the contract, and any increase added to the sold item attaches to the original contract, treating both as if they were part of the original transaction. The commentary cites consensus for discount after the subject matter is destroyed. It then illustrates through examples: if a seller adds an extra garment after the contract and the buyer discovers a defect, the buyer's right to return the defective item applies to the entire batch before possession, but only to the defective item's share after possession—even if the defect is in the added item. Similarly, if the buyer adds money to the price and the original money is reclaimed, the buyer can recover the total amount including the increase. Finally, the preemptor (shafi') has the right to preemption on the remaining part after any discount.

Key Terms
المرابحة (al-murabahah): A sale contract where the seller discloses the cost and profit margin.
التولية (al-tawliyah): A sale contract where the seller sells the item at cost price without profit.
الحط (al-hatt): Reduction or discount from the price after the contract.
الزيادة (al-ziyadah): Addition or increase either in the sold item or the price after the contract.
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): Preemption right to buy property from a co-owner.
المعيب (al-ma'ib): Defective item that gives the buyer a right of return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He may return only the defective garment.

Key Takeaway
Discount and increase in murabahah are permissible; the increase attaches to the original contract and affects defect options and preemption rights accordingly.

Adding Wine to a Sale: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Companions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on adding wine to a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding adding a forbidden item (wine) as an increase in a sale contract and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When wine is added as an increase, Abu Hanifa invalidates the sale; the two companions preserve the original sale.

This lesson examines a specific case within sales (buyu') where a buyer adds wine as an additional consideration. The Hanafi school splits: Imam Abu Hanifa treats the increase as valid but corrupting the contract, while his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, deem the increase invalid and thus leave the original sale untouched. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how invalid considerations affect contracts and which ruling is operative today.

Guided Path
1
State the Case
Identify the scenario: a buyer purchases a slave for 100, then adds a liter of wine to the price, and the seller accepts. What is the ruling?
2
Identify the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa: the increase is valid and attaches to the contract, making the entire sale fasid (corrupt). The two companions: the increase is invalid and does not attach, so the original sale remains valid.
3
Examine the Underlying Principle
The difference hinges on whether an invalid increase can attach to a valid contract. Abu Hanifa sees the increase as a valid addition of an item (even if forbidden), while the companions see wine as invalid consideration altogether.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the sale of the slave is invalid; under the companions, the sale stands and the wine is disregarded.
This affects whether the buyer must return the slave or keep it.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the two companions: the original sale remains valid. This prevents unnecessary invalidation of contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها: إذا اشترى عبداً بمائة، ثم زاده المشتري رطلاً من خمر، فقبله البائع: صحت الزيادة، وتلتحق بأصل العقد: فيفسد البيع عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما لا تصح الزيادة، ولا يفسد البيع.
Among them: if someone bought a slave for one hundred, then the buyer increased a liter of wine, and the seller accepted: the increase is valid and attaches to the original contract: so the sale is corrupted according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the increase is not valid and the sale is not corrupted.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific case: a buyer increases the price with a liter of wine after concluding a sale of a slave. According to Abu Hanifa, the increase is valid and attaches to the original contract, but because wine is a forbidden (najis) substance, the contract becomes invalid (fasid). In contrast, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the increase itself is invalid (since wine is not a proper consideration), so it does not attach to the contract, and the original sale remains valid and unaffected. This difference rests on the principle of whether an invalid increase corrupts the original contract. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the view of the two companions, as it preserves the validity of the original sale.

Key Terms
الزيادة بالخمر (al-ziyada bil-khamr): Adding wine as an additional price in a contract.
فساد البيع (fasad al-bay'): Invalidity or corruption of the sale contract due to a defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The entire sale becomes invalid.
B) The increase is valid and the sale is valid.
C) The increase is invalid and the original sale remains valid.
D) The sale is suspended pending removal of the wine.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the relied-upon view is that an invalid addition of wine does not corrupt the original sale contract.

Deferring a Previously Immediate Price
Ruling on converting a cash sale into a deferred payment with proof and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on deferring a cash price and distinguish valid from invalid deferment terms based on the type of ambiguity.

Core Idea
A seller may defer an immediate price because the debt is his right, but the term must be known; excessive ambiguity voids the deferment.

In this passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, we examine the permissibility of converting a cash sale into a deferred payment. The text explains the legal basis for this practice through analogy (qiyas) to forgiveness of debt, and establishes crucial conditions regarding the certainty of the term. We will analyze the proof, the exceptions, and the practical distinctions between excessive and approximate ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is deferring an immediate price (thaman hal) to a future date. The ruling: if the term is known, the price becomes deferred; if the term is excessively ambiguous, the deferment is void and the price remains immediate.
This is a modification of the payment term, not a new contract.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) on the seller's right to forgive (ibra) the debt entirely. Since total extinguishment is allowed, temporary postponement is allowed by a stronger analogy (from the greater to the lesser).
The text explicitly says: 'do you not see that he has the right to discharge it absolutely, so likewise temporarily.'
3
Trace the illa (effective cause)
The illa is the seller's ownership of the debt and his desire to ease for the debtor. This is a jaliyyah (clear) illa extracted by tahqiq al-manat.
The analogy applies to prices of sales and compensations for consumed items, but not to loans.
4
Distinguish between excessive and approximate ambiguity
Excessive ambiguity (jahalah mutafahishah) makes the term unknown and invalidates the deferment. Approximate ambiguity (like harvest or return of Hajj) is acceptable because the time is determinable by custom.
Examples from text: excessive – 'wind blowing', 'rain falling', 'when able'; approximate – 'harvest', 'Nowruz', 'Hajj arrival'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَن باع بثمن حال، ثم أجله أجلاً معلوماً : صار مؤجلاً . وكذا المرابحة والتولية على الكل في الزيادة، وعلى الباقي في الحط. قوله: ومن باع بثمن حال، ثم أجله أجلاً معلوماً : صار مؤجلاً؛ لأن الثمن حقه، فله أن يؤخره؛ تيسيراً على من هو عليه، ألا ترى أنه يملك إبراءه مطلقاً، فكذا مؤقتاً. وهذا كثمن البياعات، وبدل المستهلكات؛ لأن هذه الديون يجوز أن تثبت مؤجلة ابتداء، فجاز أن يطرأ عليها الأجل، بخلاف القرض. وإن أجلها إلى أجل مجهول : إن كانت الجهالة متفاحشة، كهبوب الرياح، ونزول المطر، وقدوم فلان من سفره، وإلى الميسرة: فالتأجيل باطل، والثمن حال. وإن كانت متقاربةً ،كالحصاد والدياس، والنيروز، والمهرجان، وقدوم الحاج: صح التأجيل، بمنزلة الكفالة.
And whoever sells for an immediate price, then defers it for a known term: it becomes deferred. Likewise, murabahah and tawliyah apply to the entirety in increase and to the remainder in discount. He said: 'And whoever sells for an immediate price, then defers it for a known term: it becomes deferred' because the price is his right, so he may delay it to ease for the debtor; do you not see that he has the right to discharge it absolutely, so likewise temporarily. This is like the price of sales and the compensation for consumed items, because these debts may originally be established as deferred, so deferment may occur afterwards, unlike a loan. And if he defers it to an unknown term: if the ambiguity is excessive, like wind blowing, rain falling, the arrival of someone from travel, or 'when able', then the deferment is invalid and the price remains immediate. And if it is approximate, like harvest, threshing, Nowruz, Mihrajan, or the arrival of the Hajj pilgrims, then the deferment is valid, akin to guaranty (kafalah).
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses the permissibility of converting a cash sale into a deferred payment (ta'jil). The ruling states that if a seller sells for an immediate price, then later agrees to defer it for a known term, the price becomes deferred. The proof is analogical: since the seller has the right to forgive the debt entirely, he may also postpone it temporarily by a stronger analogy. This applies to prices of sales and compensations for consumed items because such debts can originally be deferred. However, a loan (qard) is excepted because a loan deferred from the start is not permissible by analogy. The passage further distinguishes between ambiguous deferment terms: if the ambiguity is excessive (e.g., 'when it rains', 'when able'), the deferment is void and the price remains immediate; if the ambiguity is mild and approximate (e.g., 'at harvest time', 'at Nowruz'), the deferment is valid, analogous to guaranty contracts where a vague time is acceptable.

Key Terms
ثمن حال (thaman hal): Price that is due immediately at the time of contract.
تأجيل (ta'jil): Postponement of payment to a future date.
أجل معلوم (ajal ma'lum): A specified, certain future date or period.
جهالة متفاحشة (jahalah mutafahishah): Extreme ambiguity that prevents specifying the term.
كفالة (kafalah): Guaranty contract; here used as analogy for valid deferment with mild ambiguity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a seller defers an immediate price 'until the wind blows'?
A) The deferment is valid and the price becomes deferred.
B) The deferment is invalid and the price remains immediate.
C) The deferment is valid only if the buyer agrees.
D) The contract becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Deferment of an immediate price is valid if the term is known; excessive ambiguity like 'when able' invalidates it, and the price remains due immediately.

Principle of Murabahah and Tawliyah Calculations
States the basis for calculating profit and loss in murabahah and tawliyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compute the selling price in murabahah and tawliyah by applying the Hanafi rule that profit is on the total and reduction is on the remainder.

Core Idea
Profit in murabahah is on total cost; discount in tawliyah is on remainder.

This lesson presents a concise rule from Hanafi fiqh for pricing two common trust sales: murabahah (cost-plus) and tawliyah (sale at cost). Knowing this rule ensures you compute the correct selling price when there is an increase or a reduction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sale type
Determine whether the transaction is murabahah (seller adds profit) or tawliyah (seller sells at cost with reduction).
2
Check for increase or reduction
If the seller adds a profit, it is an increase (ziyadah); if they deduct an amount, it is a reduction (hutt).
3
Apply the rule
For increase: profit is calculated on the total cost price. For reduction: the reduction is subtracted from the total cost to get the remainder.
The phrase 'ala al-kull' and 'ala al-baqi' are key.
4
Compute the selling price
For murabahah: selling price = total cost + profit. For tawliyah: selling price = total cost - reduction.
Ensure the percentage is applied correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا المرابحة والتولية على الكل في الزيادة، وعلى الباقي في الحط.
Similarly, murabahah and tawliyah are based on the total in increase, and on the remainder in reduction.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This is a ruling principle for calculating pricing in two common sales: murabahah (cost-plus sale) and tawliyah (sale at cost). In murabahah, when there is an increase (e.g., profit), the profit percentage is calculated on the total cost. In tawliyah, when there is a reduction (e.g., discount), the sale price is calculated on the remaining cost after the reduction. This principle guides how to compute the selling price in these transactions.

Key Terms
مرابحة (murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and adds a specified profit.
تولية (tawliyah): A sale at exactly the cost price, no profit or loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The profit is calculated on the total cost and added to it.
C) The profit is calculated on the sale price after reduction.
D) The profit is fixed regardless of cost.

Key Takeaway
The selling price in murabahah is found by adding profit to the total cost; in tawliyah by subtracting reduction from the total cost.

Adding Invalid Item to Sale Price: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on adding invalid item to price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the addition of an invalid item to a sale price and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
An invalid addition attaches and corrupts the sale according to Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn say it does not attach.

When a buyer adds an invalid item like wine to the sale price and the seller accepts, does it corrupt the entire sale? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the addition attaches, making the price invalid and the sale fasid, while the Sahibayn argue that the addition itself is invalid ab initio and cannot affect the original valid contract. This lesson parses the reasoning behind each position and identifies the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the addition
The scenario: a buyer purchases a slave for 100 dirhams, then adds a ratl of wine to the price, and the seller accepts. Identify the core elements: a valid sale contract, a subsequent price adjustment, and an invalid item (wine) as part of the adjustment.
Wine is not considered property in Hanafi law, so it cannot be valid consideration.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa: the increase (wine) is validated by the seller's acceptance, so it attaches to the contract, altering the price. Since wine is invalid, the entire price becomes invalid, making the sale fasid.
The key is that the seller's consent makes the addition part of the price.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the wine addition is invalid from the start (wine is not mal), so the seller's acceptance cannot give it legal effect. Thus it does not attach; the original valid price remains, and the sale remains sahih.
The addition is void ab initio, so it does not alter the contract.
4
Analyse the ikhtilaf's practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the sale is fasid (voidable) and must be rescinded or re-contracted with a valid price. Under the Sahibayn, the sale is valid with the original price, and the wine addition is ignored.
This difference directly affects the parties' rights and remedies.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's view, because accepting an invalid addition indicates a change in the price that cannot be sanctioned in Shari'a.
In practice, if such a situation arises, the sale should be considered fasid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها: إذا اشترى عبداً بمائة، ثم زاده المشتري رطلاً من خمر، فقبله البائع: صحت الزيادة، وتلتحق بأصل العقد: فيفسد البيع عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما لا تصح الزيادة، ولا يفسد البيع.
And among them: if one buys a slave for one hundred, then the buyer adds a ratl of wine, and the seller accepts it: the increase is valid and attaches to the original contract, so the sale becomes corrupt according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the increase is not valid and the sale is not corrupted.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the addition of an invalid item (wine) to a sale price. The scenario: a buyer purchases a slave for 100 dirhams, then after the contract (or perhaps during it), the buyer offers an additional payment of a ratl of wine, which the seller accepts. According to Abu Hanifa, the addition (wine) becomes part of the contract, so the sale becomes fasid (corrupt) because wine is not valid consideration. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), the addition is not valid (since wine is not property), so it does not become part of the contract; thus the original sale remains valid (with the original price). The difference hinges on whether the invalid addition attaches to the contract. The mufta bihi (operative position) is that of Abu Hanifa, because the acceptance of the addition indicates a change in the price, and since wine is not permissible consideration, the sale is corrupted.

Key Terms
رطل من خمر (ratl min khamr): A measure of wine, which is an invalid (najis) and not a valid consideration in a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Both are invalid.

Key Takeaway
Adding an invalid item like wine to a sale price leads to a sale that is fasid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa), though the Sahibayn held it remains valid.

Deferment of a Spot Sale: Conditions and Exceptions
Explains the deferment of spot sales and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferring a spot sale and distinguish valid from invalid deferments based on the term and the type of debt.

Core Idea
A seller may defer a spot price, but only if the term is known and the debt is not a loan.

In this passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah, we learn that a spot sale can be turned into a deferred sale by mutual agreement, but with important conditions. The key distinction is between a sale (or compensation for damages) and a loan (qard). Understanding these rules is essential for proper contracting and avoiding riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Read the statement: 'Whoever sells for a spot price then defers it for a known term, it becomes deferred.' Recognize that the starting point is a spot sale, and the seller has the right to extend credit.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
The author gives a rational proof: the price is the seller's right, so he may delay it just as he may forgive it entirely. This is based on the principle of ownership and facilitation.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy).
3
Analyze the condition of the term
If the term is unknown, the deferment may be valid or invalid depending on the degree of uncertainty. Extreme uncertainty (e.g., 'when the wind blows') voids the deferment; moderate uncertainty (e.g., 'at harvest') is acceptable if it is commonly understood.
The standard is 'ma'qul al-ma'na' (reasonable meaning).
4
Apply the exception for qard
The passage states that every spot debt may be deferred except qard (loan). Understand why: deferring a loan would compel charity or become a riba transaction.
Qard is a gratuitous contract; forcing deferment contradicts its nature.
5
Consider the effect of death
If the debtor dies, the deferment is nullified and the debt becomes due immediately. If the creditor dies, the deferment remains. This is because the term is a right of the debtor, and his death removes that right.
This rule applies to all deferred debts except loans (which cannot be deferred anyway).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المرابحة والتولية
ومَن باع بثمن حال، ثم أجله أجلاً معلوماً : صار مؤجّلاً .
قوله: (ومن باع بثمن حال، ثم أجله أجلاً معلوماً : صار مؤجلاً)؛ لأن الثمن حقه، فله أن يؤخره؛ تيسيراً على من هو عليه، ألا ترى أنه يملك إبراءه مطلقاً، فكذا مؤقتاً.
وهذا كثمن البياعات، وبدل المستهلكات؛ لأن هذه الديون يجوز أن تثبت مؤجلة ابتداء، فجاز أن يطرأ عليها الأجل، بخلاف القرض.
- وإن أجلها إلى أجل مجهول : إن كانت الجهالة متفاحشة، كهبوب الرياح، ونزول المطر، وقدوم فلان من سفره، وإلى الميسرة: فالتأجيل باطل، والثمن حال.
وإن كانت متقاربةً ،كالحصاد والدياس، والنيروز، والمهرجان، وقدوم الحاج: صح التأجيل، بمنزلة الكفالة.
ومن مات وعليه سَلَم، أو دين سواه إلى أجل: حل ما عليه، والأصل: أن موت من عليه الدين يُبطل الأجل؛ لأن الأجل من حقه، وقد بطل حقه بموته.
وكلُّ دَيْنِ حال إذا أجله صاحبه: صار مؤجلاً، إلا القرض، فإن تأجيله لا يصح.
- وموتُ مَن له الدين: لا يُبطل الأجل ; لأن الأجل من حق المطلوب، وهو حي، وليس لورثته أن يطالبوه قبل الأجل.
قوله: (وكلُّ دين حال إذا أجله صاحبه: صار مؤجلاً، إلا القرض: فإن تأجيله لا يصح ) ; لأنه اصطناع معروف، وفي جواز تأجيله: جبر على اصطناع المعروف.
ولأنه إعارة وصلَةٌ في الابتداء، حتى يصح بلفظ الإعارة، ولا يملكه من لا يملك التبرع، كالصبي والوصي، ومعاوضة في الانتهاء: فعلى اعتبار الابتداء: لا يلزم التأجيلُ فيه، أي لمن أجله : إبطاله، كما في الإعارة; إذ لا إجبار في التبرع.
وعلى اعتبار الانتهاء : لا يصح تأجيله; لأنه يصير بيع الدراهم بالدراهم نسيئة، وهو رباً، والله أعلم.
Chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. Whoever sells for a spot price then defers it for a known term, it becomes deferred. He said: (Whoever sells for a spot price then defers it for a known term, it becomes deferred) because the price is his right, so he may delay it to facilitate for the one who owes it. Do you not see that he has the right to absolve him absolutely, so likewise temporarily? This applies to the price of sales and the compensation for consumable items, because these debts may be established as deferred initially, so it is permissible for deferment to intervene upon them, unlike a loan. And if he defers it for an unknown term: if the ignorance is extreme, like the blowing of winds, the falling of rain, the arrival of so-and-so from his travel, or until easy circumstances, then the deferment is invalid and the price is spot. If the ignorance is moderate, like harvest, threshing, Nowruz, Mihrajan, or the arrival of the Hajj pilgrims, the deferment is valid, like guarantee. Whoever dies while owing a salam or other debt to a term, what is owed becomes due immediately, and the principle is that the death of the debtor nullifies the deferment, because the deferment is his right, and his right is nullified by his death. Every spot debt, if its owner defers it, becomes deferred, except for a loan, for its deferment is not valid. The death of the one to whom the debt is owed does not nullify the deferment, because the deferment is the right of the one who is owed, and he is alive, and his heirs may not demand it before the term. He said: (Every spot debt, if its owner defers it, becomes deferred, except for a loan: its deferment is not valid) because it is a form of benevolence, and allowing its deferment would compell benevolence. And because it is a loan and a gift initially, such that it is valid with the wording of loan, and those who cannot donate own it not, like a child or executor, and it is a compensation at the end. So from the perspective of the beginning, deferment is not binding, meaning he may invalidate it, just as in a loan, because there is no compulsion in benevolence. From the perspective of the end, its deferment is not valid, because it becomes a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit, which is riba. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the deferment of spot sales. The author first states the ruling: if a seller sells for a spot price and then later defers payment to a known term, the price becomes deferred. The proof is that the price is the seller's right, so he may delay it just as he may absolve it entirely. This applies to prices in sales and compensation for destroyed items (like lost goods) because these can initially be set as deferred. However, qard (loan) is an exception; its deferment is invalid because a loan is a form of charity (qard is a contract of benevolence). The author then discusses the condition of the term: if the term is unknown with extreme uncertainty (e.g., 'when the wind blows'), the deferment is void; if the uncertainty is moderate (e.g., 'at harvest time'), it is valid by analogy to guarantee (kafala). Next, the effect of death: if the debtor dies, the debt becomes immediately due because the deferment was a concession for him and ends with his death. If the creditor dies, the deferment remains because it is the debtor's right. The commentary further explains the qard exception: deferring a loan would compel benevolence (since qard is a charitable loan) or it would become a sale of currency on credit (riba). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one stated: deferment is valid for sales but not for loans.

Key Terms
أجل (ajal): A specified future time for payment of a debt.
قرض (qard): A loan of fungible items to be repaid in kind; a charitable contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is true regarding deferment of a spot sale?
A) Deferment is always valid regardless of the term.
B) Deferment is invalid if the term is extremely uncertain.
C) Deferment of a qard is valid.
D) Death of the creditor nullifies the deferment.

Key Takeaway
Deferment of a spot sale is valid with a known term, but never for a loan (qard).

Deferring a Demand Debt: General Rule and Qard Exception
States ruling on deferring demand debts with an exception for qard and provides dual talil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferring a demand debt and explain why deferring a loan (qard) is invalid using the two considerations from the text.

Core Idea
A demand debt can be deferred by mutual agreement, but delaying repayment of a loan (qard) is invalid because it would constitute riba.

This passage from the chapter on Murabaha and Tawliya presents a key principle: any demand debt can be deferred if the creditor agrees, except for loans (qard). The commentary provides a dual-reasoning to explain why deferring a qard is prohibited. Understanding this ruling is essential for distinguishing permissible debt restructuring from prohibited riba-based transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize the subject: deferring a demand debt (ta'jīl al-dayn al-ḥāl). The general rule states it becomes deferred (ṣāra mu'ajjalan).
The act is a modification of the debt contract by agreement.
2
Locate the exception
The text explicitly exempts qard (loan): 'illa al-qarḍ, fa-inna ta'jīlahu lā yaṣiḥḥ'. The deferment of a loan is not valid.
Qard is a transfer of ownership with a promise to repay in kind.
3
Follow the first consideration: inception as beneficence
Qard begins as a charitable act (ṣinā'at ma'rūf). Compelling deferment would be compelling charity, which is impermissible.
This parallels i'ārah (lending use) where the lender can recall the item.
4
Follow the second consideration: conclusion as exchange
Upon repayment, qard becomes an exchange. Deferring repayment makes it a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit, which is ribā.
The prohibition of ribā overrides any agreement.
5
Synthesize: why both perspectives lead to invalidity
From either angle—charitable inception or exchange conclusion—deferment is invalid. Thus the ruling is categorical.
No ikhtilāf among Hanafis on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المرابحة والتولية
وكلُّ دَيْنِ حال إذا أجله صاحبه: صار مؤجلاً، إلا القرض، فإن تأجيله لا يصح.
- وموتُ مَن له الدين: لا يُبطل الأجل ؛ لأن الأجل من حق المطلوب، وهو حي، وليس لورثته أن يطالبوه قبل الأجل.
*
قوله: (وكلُّ دين حال إذا أجله صاحبه: صار مؤجلاً، إلا القرض: فإن تأجيله لا يصح ) ؛ لأنه اصطناع معروف، وفي جواز تأجيله: جبر على اصطناع المعروف.
ولأنه إعارة وصلَةٌ في الابتداء، حتى يصح بلفظ الإعارة، ولا يملكه من لا يملك التبرع، كالصبي والوصي، ومعاوضة في الانتهاء: فعلى اعتبار الابتداء: لا يلزم التأجيلُ فيه، أي لمن أجله : إبطاله، كما في الإعارة؛ إذ لا إجبار في التبرع.
وعلى اعتبار الانتهاء : لا تأجيله؛ لأنه يصير بيع الدراهم بالدراهم نسيئة، وهو رباً، والله أعلم.
Chapter of Murabaha and Tawliya
Every demand debt, if its owner defers it, becomes deferred, except for the loan (qard), for its deferment is not valid.
- The death of the one to whom the debt is owed does not nullify the term, because the term is a right of the debtor, who is alive, and his heirs may not demand it before the term.
*
His saying: (Every demand debt, if its owner defers it, becomes deferred, except for the loan: for its deferment is not valid) because it is an act of beneficence, and permitting its deferment would compel beneficence.
And because it is a loan and a gift in the beginning, such that it is valid with the wording of a loan, and it is not owned by one who cannot give charity, like a minor and a guardian, and it is a exchange in the end. So on the basis of the beginning, deferment is not binding on it, meaning for the one who defers it it is invalid, as in a loan, for there is no compulsion in charity.
And on the basis of the end, its deferment is not valid, because it becomes a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit, which is riba. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its rationale from the chapter on Murabaha and Tawliya. The matn states a general principle: any demand debt (dayn hal) becomes deferred (mu'ajjal) if the creditor (saahib) agrees to defer it. An exception is made for the loan (qard): deferring a qard is not valid. The commentary explains the reasoning using two considerations (i'tibaran). First, qard is an act of beneficence (sinā'at ma'ruf) in its inception; compelling deferment would be compelling beneficence, which is not allowed. Second, qard is like a charitable loan (i'arah) in the beginning—it is valid with the wording of i'arah and not owned by someone who cannot give charity, such as a minor or guardian. In the end, it becomes an exchange. From the perspective of the beginning, deferment is not binding and can be rescinded, similar to a loan of objects. From the perspective of the end, deferment is invalid because it would become a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit (nasī'ah), which is riba. Thus, deferring a qard is prohibited to avoid riba while preserving the charitable nature of the transaction.

Key Terms
دَيْن حَال (dayn ḥāl): A debt that is immediately due and payable.
تَأْجِيل (ta'jīl): Postponing the due date of a debt with the creditor's consent.
قَرْض (qarḍ): A loan of fungible items (like money) given with the intent of being repaid in kind.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is deferring a loan (qard) not valid in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the borrower would be harmed by the delay.
B) Because it would become a sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit, which is riba.
C) Because loans cannot be modified after the contract.
D) Because the lender may change his mind.

Key Takeaway
Deferring a qard is invalid in the Hanafi school because it transforms the charitable loan into a sale on credit, which is riba, and violates the principle that beneficence cannot be compelled.

Definition and Prohibition of Riba
Defines riba linguistically and legally, cites prohibition from Quran and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define riba linguistically and legally, identify its prohibition as haram, and state the two types (riba al-fadl and riba al-nasi'ah) with evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Riba is any invalid exchange involving unjustified increase or delay, prohibited by definitive texts.

Riba (usury/interest) is a major sin in Islam, and its prohibition is well-established. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definition: riba is not only about surplus (riba al-fadl) but also about delay (riba al-nasi'ah) in exchanges of same commodities. We'll explore the linguistic and legal meanings, and then see the Quranic and hadith evidence that makes it haram.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic vs legal meaning
First, note that linguistically riba means 'increase' (ziyada). Legally (shar'an), it is an 'invalid contract by description'—meaning the contract itself is defective regardless of whether an increase occurs.
The legal definition is broader than the literal one, covering cases without increase.
2
Identify the components of the legal definition
The definition mentions 'invalid contract by description' (عقد فاسد بصفة). This means the contract is flawed due to certain characteristics, such as delay or excess in ribawi items.
The description (sifa) refers to the prohibited element (increase or delay).
3
Recognize the example illustrating riba without increase
The text gives the sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit (nasī'ah): even with equal amounts, the delay alone makes it riba. This is riba al-nasi'ah.
This example shows that delay (nasī'ah) is a prohibited element.
4
Locate the Quranic and hadith evidence
The Quran (al-Baqarah 2:275) is cited: 'And forbade riba.' The hadith from al-Tabarani warns that consuming one dirham of riba is worse than thirty-three acts of fornication, and flesh nourished from haram deserves the Fire.
The hadith's chain is discussed in the footnote; many scholars consider it authentic.
5
Appreciate the severity of the prohibition
The hadith's strong language emphasizes the gravity of riba. Understanding this helps internalize why scholars are strict about ribawi transactions.
The severity is not just a warning but a motivation to avoid all forms of riba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الربا
الربا في اللغة هو : الزيادة. وفي الشرع : عبارة عن عقد فاسد بصفة، سواء كان هناك زيادة، أو لا، ألا ترى أن بيع الدراهم بالدراهم نسيئة: رباً، وليس فيه زيادة. والربا حرام بالكتاب والسنة، أما الكتاب : فقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَحَرَّمَ الربوا . البقرة / ٢٧٥ .
وأما السنة : فقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أكل درهم واحد من الربا: أشد من ثلاث وثلاثين زنيةٌ يزنيها الرجل، ومَن نَبَتَ لحمه من حرام: فالنار أولى به»(1).
(۱) عزاه ابن حجر الهيتمي في الزواجر ۲۲۷/۱ للطبراني في الصغير (٢٢٤)، والأوسط (٢٦٨٢، ٢٩٤٤)، مسند الإمام أحمد (۲۱۹٥٧)، وفي الحديث كلام في رفعه ووقفه، وفي ثبوته، وقد صححه جماعة كبيرة، وضعفه البعض، وقال العراقي في تخريج الإحياء رجاله ثقات وينظر المصنف لابن أبي شيبة ٣١٥/١١، وتعليقات فضيلة المحقق الشيخ محمد ،عوامة، وفيض القدير للمناوي ٥٢٤/٣.
Chapter of Riba
Riba linguistically is increase. And legally it is an expression for an invalid contract by description, whether there is increase or not. Do you not see that the sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit is riba, and there is no increase in it. And riba is prohibited by the Book and the Sunnah. As for the Book: His saying, Exalted is He: {And forbade riba} [al-Baqarah 2:275]. And as for the Sunnah: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Consuming one dirham of riba is more severe than thirty-three acts of fornication committed by a man, and whoever's flesh grows from unlawful [wealth], the Fire is more deserving of him.' (1) [Footnote: Ibn Hajar al-Haytami attributed it in al-Zawajir to al-Tabarani in al-Saghir, al-Awsat, Musnad Ahmad; there is discussion on its authenticity; many authenticated it, some weakened it; al-Iraqi said its narrators are trustworthy...]
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Riba provides a definition and prohibition. Linguistically, riba means increase (ziyada). Legally (shar'an), it is defined as any invalid contract (aql fāsid) characterized by certain conditions (bi-sifatin), regardless of whether there is an actual increase or not. An example is selling dirhams for dirhams on credit (nasī'ah)—even though the principal amounts are equal, the delay makes it riba. The prohibition is established by the Qur'an (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:275) and Sunnah. The hadith quoted emphasizes the severity of consuming riba, comparing it to multiple acts of fornication and warning that flesh nourished from unlawful earnings deserves Hellfire. The footnote discusses the hadith's chain and scholars' opinions on its authenticity, with many considering it authentic (sahih) despite some weakness.

Key Terms
الرِّبا (al-ribā): Linguistically: increase. Legally: an invalid contract by description, whether there is increase or not, such as selling dirhams for dirhams on credit.
زِيَادَة (ziyāda): Increase or addition; the linguistic meaning of riba.
عَقْد فَاسِد (aql fāsid): An invalid contract (due to a defect in the subject matter or consideration).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes the sale of dirhams for dirhams on credit riba even though there is no increase?
A) The promise of future payment.
B) The absence of a written contract.
C) The delay (nasī'ah) in exchange.
D) The involvement of money.

Key Takeaway
Riba is haram and includes both increase and delay in exchanges of certain items, as defined by the Hanafi school.

Hanafi Definition and Prohibition of Riba with 'Illa Dispute
Defines riba, cites prohibition, and contrasts Hanafi 'illa with Shafi'i/Maliki.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of riba, identify its prohibition proofs, and explain the Hanafi 'illa for riba while contrasting it with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Riba is forbidden in all measurable/weighable items sold by genus with excess – the Hanafi 'illa is measure/weight with genus.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi stance on riba, beginning with its linguistic and legal definition. After establishing the prohibition from Quran and Sunnah, the text delves into the central dispute: what exactly triggers riba? The answer determines whether ordinary business transactions like selling lime or iron ore fall under the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Define riba linguistically and legally
Extract the Hanafi definition from the text: riba is a defective contract, whether increase exists or not. Note that credit sale of same currency is riba without increase.
The definition sets the scope for the prohibition.
2
Identify the sources of prohibition
Locate the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:275: 'wa harrama al-riba') and the hadith about the severity of riba and the curse on participants.
Both sources are qati' (definitive) in the Hanafi view.
3
State the Hanafi ruling and 'illa
The ruling: riba is haram in every makil (measurable) and mawzun (weighable) item when sold for its own genus with excess. The 'illa is kail (measure) or wazn (weight) combined with genus (jins). A more comprehensive term is qadr (quantity).
This 'illa is broader than other schools.
4
Compare with Shafi'i and Maliki 'illas
Shafi'i 'illa: edibility (tam) with genus for foodstuffs, and monetariness (thamaniyya) for currencies. Maliki 'illa: sustenance (iqtitat) and storability (idikhar) with genus. Note the narrowing of the 'illa.
Identify which items become excluded in each school.
5
Apply to a concrete case
The text gives the example of selling nura (lime) – a non-edible, non-storable mineral – by volume: Hanafis prohibit it due to kail + jins; Shafi'is and Malikis permit it. Practice applying the 'illa to other items like iron ore or cement.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الربا
الربا في اللغة هو : الزيادة. وفي الشرع : عبارة عن عقد فاسد بصفة، سواء كان هناك زيادة، أو لا، ألا ترى أن بيع الدراهم بالدراهم نسيئة: رباً، وليس فيه زيادة. والربا حرام بالكتاب والسنة، أما الكتاب : فقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَحَرَّمَ الربوا ﴾ البقرة / ٢٧٥ . وأما السنة : فقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «أكل درهم واحد من الربا: أشد من ثلاث وثلاثين زنيةٌ يزنيها الرجل، ومَن نَبَتَ لحمه من حرام: فالنار أولى به». وقال ابن مسعود: «آكل الربا، ومؤكله، وكاتبه، وشاهده إذا علموا به : ملعونون على لسان محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى يوم القيامة». كذا في «النهاية».
قال رحمه الله: (الربا محرَّم في كل مكيل وموزون إذا بيع بجنسه متفاضلاً)، سواء كان مأكولاً، أو غير مأكول. * قوله: (فالعلة فيه: الكيلُ مع الجنس، أو الوزن مع الجنس). ويقال: القدر مع الجنس، وهو أشمل ؛ لأنه يتناول الكيل والوزن معاً، بخلاف لفظ : الكيل، فإنه لا يتناول الوزن، ولفظ الوزن: لا يتناول الكيل، وأما لفظ : القدر فيشملهما معاً. وقال الشافعي): العلة: الطعم مع الجنس في المطعومات، والثمنية في الأثمان. وقال مالك(۳): العلة : الاقتيات، والادخار مع الجنس. وفائدته : فيمن باع قفير نُورة بقفيزين نُورةً: لا يجوز عندنا؛ لوجود الكيل مع الجنس.
Chapter of Riba. Riba linguistically is: increase. And in Shari'ah: it is an expression of a defective contract with a description, whether there is increase or not. Do you not see that selling dirhams for dirhams on credit is riba, and there is no increase in it. And riba is forbidden by the Book and the Sunnah. As for the Book: His saying, Exalted is He: 'And He forbade usury' (al-Baqarah 2:275). And as for the Sunnah: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Eating one dirham of riba is more severe than thirty-three acts of fornication that a man commits, and whoever's flesh grows from ill-gotten gains, the Fire is more deserving of him.' And Ibn Mas'ud said: 'The consumer of riba, its feeder, its writer, and its witness, if they know about it, are cursed on the tongue of Muhammad, peace be upon him, until the Day of Judgment.' Thus in 'al-Nihayah'. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (Riba is forbidden in every measurable (makil) and weighable (mawzun) item if it is sold for its own genus with excess), whether it is edible or not. * His saying: (So the cause ('illa) in it is: measure (kail) with genus, or weight (wazn) with genus). And it is said: quantity (qadr) with genus, and it is more comprehensive because it includes both measure and weight together, unlike the term 'kail' for it does not include weight, and the term 'wazn' does not include measure. And al-Shafi'i said: The cause is: taste (tam) with genus in foodstuffs, and monetariness (thamaniyya) in currencies. And Malik said: The cause is: sustenance (iqtitat) and storage (idikhar) with genus. And its benefit: in the case of one who sells a qafiz of nura (lime) for two qafiz of nura: it is not permissible according to us due to the existence of measure with genus.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Riba presents the Hanafi definition and prohibition of riba, followed by the key jurisprudential dispute over the effective cause ('illa) that triggers riba in sales. The passage begins by defining riba linguistically as 'increase' and legally as a defective contract (even if no increase exists, as in credit sales of same currency). It then establishes the prohibition from the Quran (al-Baqarah 2:275) and Sunnah (the severe hadith comparing riba to multiple acts of zina, and the curse on participants). The author then states the Hanafi ruling: riba is forbidden in all measurable (makil) and weighable (mawzun) items when sold for their own genus with excess (tafadul). The 'illa is measure or weight combined with genus. A more comprehensive term is 'quantity' (qadr) which covers both. The passage then contrasts the Shafi'i position: 'illa is edibility (tam) with genus for foodstuffs and monetariness (thamaniyya) for currencies. The Maliki position is sustenance (iqtitat) and storability (idikhar) with genus. The practical difference (thamar al-khilaf) is illustrated with the example of selling lime (nura) – a non-edible, non-storable mineral – for its own genus in excess: Hanafis rule it invalid due to measure with genus, while Shafi'is and Malikis would permit it since it lacks their respective 'illas. This highlights how the 'illa definition directly affects which transactions are considered ribawi.

Key Terms
الربا (al-riba): In this text: a defective contract (عقد فاسد بصفة) that is prohibited even if no actual increase occurs, such as credit sale of same currency.
العِلَّة (al-illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that triggers the legal ruling; here it determines when riba applies in sales.
الكيل (al-kail): Measurement by volume; a standard means of quantifying commodities in trade.
الوزن (al-wazn): Measurement by weight; used for commodities like gold, silver.
الطعم (al-tam): Edibility; according to Shafi'i, it is part of the 'illa for riba in foodstuffs.
الثمنية (al-thamaniyya): Monetariness; the quality of being used as money (thaman).
الاقتيات (al-iqtitat): Sustenance; being a staple food that sustains life, according to Maliki school.
الادخار (al-idikhar): Storability; ability to be stored for long periods, Maliki condition for riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the sale of a qafiz of lime for two qafiz of lime invalid?
A) Because lime is not edible.
B) Because lime is sold by measure and the excess is riba.
C) Because lime is a staple food.
D) Because lime is currency.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi 'illa for riba is measure/weight with genus, making all volume- or weight-based commodities subject to the prohibition, regardless of edibility.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
The Hanafi Cause of Riba: Measurement and Weight
Defines riba and explains Hanafi cause with inter-madhhab comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi cause of riba and compare it with the Shafi'i cause, applying the difference to concrete transactions.

Core Idea
Riba's cause is measurement/weight with same genus — not edibility — so lime is ribawi but watermelon is not.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira defines riba and the Hanafi illah, contrasting it with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. You'll learn why a bag of lime falls under riba but a watermelon does not, and how the choice of illah changes the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of riba
The passage states riba is prohibited in every measured (makīl) or weighed (mawzūn) item sold with its genus (jins) with excess (tafāḍul).
The three conditions: genus, measurement/weight, and excess.
2
Extract the Hanafi illah
The cause is either measurement with genus or weight with genus. The term 'qadr' (quantity) is more comprehensive as it covers both.
Al-Qadr includes both kayl and wazn.
3
Contrast the Shafi'i illah
Shafi'i holds the cause is edibility (ṭuʿm) with genus for foodstuffs, and thamaniyyah (currency-value) for gold and silver.
Based on hadith of six commodities.
4
Observe the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical differences: lime (measured) is ribawi for Hanafi but not for Shafi'i; watermelon (not measured) is not ribawi for Hanafi but is for Shafi'i due to edibility.
The same transaction gets opposite rulings.
5
Reflect on the Maliki position
Maliki holds the cause is being a staple (iqtīāt) and storable (iddikhār) with genus. This is mentioned but not elaborated.
Another school with a different illah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الربا
الربا محرم في كل مكيل أو موزون إذا بيع بجنسه متفاضلاً. فالعلة فيه: الكيل مع الجنس، أو الوزن مع الجنس.
وقال ابن مسعود: «آكل الربا، ومؤكله، وكاتبه، وشاهده إذا علموا به: ملعونون على لسان محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى يوم القيامة». كذا في «النهاية».
قال رحمه الله: (الربا محرم في كل مكيل وموزون إذا بيع بجنسه متفاضلاً)، سواء كان مأكولاً أو غير مأكول.
قوله: (فالعلة فيه: الكيل مع الجنس، أو الوزن مع الجنس). ويقال: القدر مع الجنس، وهو أشمل؛ لأنه يتناول الكيل والوزن معاً، بخلاف لفظ الكيل، فإنه لا يتناول الوزن، ولفظ الوزن لا يتناول الكيل، وأما لفظ القدر فيشملهما معاً.
وقال الشافعي: العلة: الطعم مع الجنس في المطعومات، والثمنية في الأثمان.
وقال مالك: العلة: الاقتيات والادخار مع الجنس.
وفائدته: فيمن باع قفير نورة بقفيزين نورةً: لا يجوز عندنا؛ لوجود الكيل مع الجنس. وعند الشافعي: يجوز؛ لعدم الطعم.
وكذا يجوز بيع بطيخة ببطيختين، وبيضة ببيضتين، وحفنة بحفنتين عندنا؛ لعدم الكيل. ولا يجوز عنده؛ لوجود الطعم.
Chapter of Riba. Riba is prohibited in every measured or weighed [item] when sold with its genus with excess. The cause in it is: measurement with genus, or weight with genus. Ibn Mas'ud said: 'The consumer of riba, its feeder, its writer, and its witness—if they know it—are cursed on the tongue of Muhammad (peace be upon him) until the Day of Judgment.' Thus in al-Nihaya. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Riba is prohibited in every measured and weighed [item] when sold with its genus with excess), whether it is edible or not edible. His statement: (The cause in it is measurement with genus, or weight with genus). And it is said: quantity (al-qadr) with genus, and it is more comprehensive because it includes both measurement and weight, unlike the term measurement, for it does not include weight, and the term weight does not include measurement, but the term quantity includes them both. Al-Shafi'i said: The cause is edibility (al-tu'm) with genus in foodstuffs, and price-ness (al-thamaniyyah) in precious metals (al-athman). Malik said: The cause is being a staple (al-iqtiat) and storable (al-iddikhar) with genus. Its benefit (application): Whoever sells a qafiz of nurah (lime) for two qafiz of nurah: it is not permissible according to us (Hanafis) due to the existence of measurement with genus. According to al-Shafi'i: it is permissible due to the absence of edibility. Similarly, the sale of a watermelon for two watermelons, an egg for two eggs, a handful (hafna) for two handfuls is permissible according to us due to the absence of measurement. And it is not permissible according to him due to the existence of edibility.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the cause (illah) of riba and compares it with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. The Hanafi school defines riba as prohibited in all items sold by measure (mukil) or weight (mawzun) when exchanged with the same genus and excess. The cause is the combination of measurement/weight with the same genus. The term 'quantity' (qadr) is preferred as it covers both measure and weight. The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud emphasizes the severe prohibition. The Shafi'i school argues the cause is edibility (tu'm) in foodstuffs and currency-value (thamaniyyah) in gold and silver. The Maliki school defines it as being a staple and storable (iqtiat and iddikhar). The practical difference is shown in examples: selling lime (nurah) for more lime is invalid for Hanafis (due to measurement) but valid for Shafi'is (no edibility). Selling watermelon, eggs, or handfuls is valid for Hanafis (no measurement) but invalid for Shafi'is (edibility present). This highlights the concrete impact of differing legal causes.

Key Terms
ربا (ribā): An excess in a barter transaction of items of the same type, measured or weighed.
مكيل (makīl): An item sold by volume measurement (e.g., grains, liquids).
موزون (mawzūn): An item sold by weight (e.g., metals, solids).
علة (ʿillah): The effective legal cause that triggers the prohibition of riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is selling a container of honey (measured by volume) for twice as much honey prohibited?
A) Because honey is edible
B) Because honey is measured and same genus with excess
C) Because honey is a currency
D) Because honey is a staple food

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines riba through measurement/weight with genus, a broader cause than the Shafi'i edibility criterion.
